<p><b>Louisa Nécib Cadamuro</b> (<small>French pronunciation: ​</small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_French" title="Help:IPA for French">[luiza neˈsib]</a></span>; born 23 January 1987) is a retired <a href="/wiki/List_of_France_women%27s_international_footballers" title="List of France women's international footballers">French women's international footballer</a>. She spent the majority of her career at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais_(ladies)" title="Olympique Lyonnais (ladies)">Lyon</a>, amassing eighteen titles with the French club over a nine-year span. She played as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">central attacking midfielder</a> and is described as a "gifted <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">playmaker</a>" who "possesses superb technique".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_fifa_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-necib_fifa-2">[2]</a></sup> Nécib is also known for her "elegant possession, sublime passing skills, and cultured touch on the ball".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_cbc_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-necib_cbc-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>She has been labeled by the French media as "the female <a href="/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane" title="Zinedine Zidane">Zidane</a>" - like Zinedine Zidane, she has Algerian ancestry, grew up in Marseille and possesses immense skill, especially as a playmaker with an eye for goal. As such, she has been nicknamed "Ziza", a variant of Zidane's "Zizou".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_fifa_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-necib_fifa-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_marseille_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-necib_marseille-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_20minutes_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-necib_20minutes-6">[6]</a></sup> In an interview with FIFA.com just before the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_Olympics_soccer" title="2012 Olympics soccer">2012 Olympics</a>, she alluded to the comparison, saying, "Zidane is a role model for me. He was always the player that I most enjoyed watching. The comparison was made frequently when I was starting out, and now, as the years pass, it happens less and less often. But I wouldn't say I’m tired of it." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> She often attempts to downplay the comparison, though, stating "Being compared to Zidane is really nice, but I don’t think it can harm me because I’ve been hearing it since I was very young. It always makes me proud, but as I always say, I don’t think you can compare anyone to him. He’s unique".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_ray_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-necib_ray-8">[8]</a></sup> While training at the Clairefontaine academy in 2004, Nécib met Zidane, who was at the training center in preparation for <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="2006 FIFA World Cup qualification">qualifying for the 2006 World Cup</a> (the finals would eventually be his last act as a professional). The two players exchanged shirts, and the shirt Nécib acquired from Zidane is currently in the possession of her father.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_federation_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-necib_federation-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nécib began her football career playing for local youth clubs in her hometown of <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a>, such as Union Sportive Marseille and Celtic de Marseille. With the latter club, she made her senior team debut in 2003 and, in the following season, helped the club win the Division 3 Féminine. In 2004, Nécib was selected to attend <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clairefontaine" title="Clairefontaine">CNFE Clairefontaine</a>, the women's section of the Clairefontaine academy. She spent two years at the training center, and in 2006, departed for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montpellier_HSC_(Ladies)" title="Montpellier HSC (Ladies)">Montpellier</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Division_1_F%C3%A9minine" title="Division 1 Féminine">Division 1 Féminine</a>. In her only season with Montpellier, Nécib helped the team win the 2006–07 edition of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Challenge_de_France" title="Challenge de France">Challenge de France</a>. After departing Montpellier, she joined <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais_(Ladies)" title="Olympique Lyonnais (Ladies)">Lyon</a>. Since joining the club, Nécib has won a slew of trophies, which include four league titles, one Challenge de France, and one <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Women%27s_Champions_League" title="UEFA Women's Champions League">UEFA Women's Champions League</a> title. For her performances during the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Division_1_F%C3%A9minine" title="2008–09 Division 1 Féminine">2008–09 season</a>, she was named the <a href="/wiki/National_Union_of_Professional_Footballers" title="National Union of Professional Footballers">National Union of Professional Footballers</a> (UNFP) <a href="/wiki/Troph%C3%A9es_UNFP_du_football#Player_of_the_Year_3" title="Trophées UNFP du football">Female Player of the Year</a>.</p>
<p>Nécib is a former French women's youth international having represented her nation at all levels for which she was eligible. At under-19 level, she played on the teams that reached the <a href="/wiki/2004_UEFA_Women%27s_Under-19_Championship" title="2004 UEFA Women's Under-19 Championship">2004</a> and <a href="/wiki/2005_UEFA_Women%27s_Under-19_Championship" title="2005 UEFA Women's Under-19 Championship">2005</a> editions of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Women%27s_Under-19_Championship" title="UEFA Women's Under-19 Championship">UEFA Women's Under-19 Championship</a>. With the under-20 team, Nécib played at the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_U-20_Women%27s_World_Championship" title="2006 FIFA U-20 Women's World Championship">2006 FIFA U-20 Women's World Championship</a> scoring a goal in the group stage against <a href="/wiki/Argentina_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Argentina women's national football team">Argentina</a> as France reached the quarter-finals. Prior to playing in the U-20 Women's World Cup, Nécib made her senior international debut in February 2005 in a friendly match against <a href="/wiki/Norway_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Norway women's national football team">Norway</a>. Two years later in March 2007, Nécib scored her first senior international goal in a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Women%27s_Euro_2009_qualifying" title="UEFA Women's Euro 2009 qualifying">UEFA Women's Euro 2009 qualifying</a> victory over <a href="/wiki/Greece_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Greece women's national football team">Greece</a>. She has participated in five major international tournaments for her country; the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Women%27s_Euro_2005" title="UEFA Women's Euro 2005">2005</a> and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Women%27s_Euro_2009" title="UEFA Women's Euro 2009">2009</a> editions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_Women%27s_Euro" title="UEFA Women's Euro">UEFA Women's Euro</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2011 FIFA Women's World Cup">2011</a> and <a href="/wiki/2015_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2015 FIFA Women's World Cup">2015 FIFA Women's World Cup</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a>. In the latter competition, Nécib acted as the <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">playmaker</a> and contributed to the team that finished in fourth place.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisa_Cadamuro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Nécib was born on 23 January 1987 in the city of <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Marseille</a> to parents of <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algerian</a> origin. Her father had emigrated to France from <a href="/wiki/Biskra" title="Biskra">Biskra</a>, while her mother had come from <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Nécib was raised in Busserine, a quarter located in the northern suburbs of the <a href="/wiki/14th_arrondissement_of_Marseille" title="14th arrondissement of Marseille">14th arrondissement of Marseille</a> and has a brother and sister.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_marseille_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-necib_marseille-4">[4]</a></sup> After signing with Lyon, Nécib enrolled at the <a href="/wiki/Claude_Bernard_University_Lyon_1" title="Claude Bernard University Lyon 1">Université Lyon 1</a> with hopes of completing her undergraduate studies in <i>Sciences et techniques des activités physiques et sportives</i> (STAP) (English: Science and Technology of Sport and Physical Activity).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_marseille_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-necib_marseille-4">[4]</a></sup> She developed an interest in <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> at a young age, prior to which she trained in <a href="/wiki/Gymnastics" title="Gymnastics">gymnastics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_laprovence2_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-necib_laprovence2-11">[11]</a></sup> She, initially, did not look at the future prospects of women's football and played mainly for recreation with males stating "I'd always played with the boys in my neighborhood" and "I didn't plan to join a club because, to be honest, I didn't know girls' teams existed. Then, one day I found out there was a club in the 14th arrondissement and I signed up".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_fifa_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-necib_fifa-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2016, she married footballer <a href="/wiki/Liassine_Cadamuro-Benta%C3%AFba" title="Liassine Cadamuro-Bentaïba">Liassine Cadamuro-Bentaïba</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisa_Cadamuro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisa_Cadamuro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:30%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"These comparisons do not bother me. To be compared with <i>Zizou</i> is a pride. But there is no comparison to make. I am myself."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;"><small>Nécib on the comparisons to <a href="/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane" title="Zinedine Zidane">Zinedine Zidane</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_laprovence2_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-necib_laprovence2-11">[11]</a></sup></small></cite></div>
<p>Nécib began her career as a youth player for her hometown club Union Sportive de Marseille.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_laprovence1_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-necib_laprovence1-12">[12]</a></sup> After spending two years at the club, she signed on with nearby Celtic de Marseille. Nécib spent six months developing in the academy and, in April 2002, she was selected to attend the under-16 female National Cup representing her <a href="/wiki/Provence-Alpes-C%C3%B4te_d%27Azur" title="Provence-Alpes-Côte d'Azur">region</a>. The competition served as a training camp for the Centre National de Formation et d'Entraînement (CNFE) (English: National Center for Education and Training) located at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clairefontaine" title="Clairefontaine">Clairefontaine</a> academy in <a href="/wiki/Clairefontaine-en-Yvelines" title="Clairefontaine-en-Yvelines">Clairefontaine-en-Yvelines</a>. The initiative to allow women to train at the famous national center came about in the 1990s due to the fact that it had quickly become a high-level training facility for male football players. As a result of allowing female football players to train at the academy, younger women were afforded the same benefits from the facilities offered by Clairefontaine as the men. At the National Cup, Nécib impressed and was given an award by coaches for possessing the best shot of any player.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> After the competition, she returned to Celtic.</p>
<p>At the age of 16, Nécib was promoted to the senior team by coach Yohan Silvy in the latter part of the 2002–03 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_laprovence1_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-necib_laprovence1-12">[12]</a></sup> While at the club, Nécib was teammates with future national teammate <a href="/wiki/Caroline_Pizzala" title="Caroline Pizzala">Caroline Pizzala</a>. In the 2003–04 season, Nécib flourished and helped the club reach the Division 3 Féminine league final where they faced the women's team of professional men's club <a href="/wiki/Le_Mans_FC" title="Le Mans FC">Le Mans</a>. In the tie, Nécib started and played the full match as Celtic cruised to a 4–1 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The result promoted the club to the Division 2 Féminine, the second division of French women's football. Nécib's performance that season attracted numerous attention, which resulted in her being nicknamed <i>Titou</i> as homage to <a href="/wiki/Zinedine_Zidane" title="Zinedine Zidane">Zinedine Zidane</a>, who is nicknamed <i>Zizou</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_laprovence1_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-necib_laprovence1-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>After three years with Celtic, in July 2004, Nécib was selected to attend the CNFE academy at Clairefontaine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_marseille_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-necib_marseille-4">[4]</a></sup> She initially struggled to adapt at the center admitting "the first year was really hard because I was so far from my family. I almost gave up".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_fifa_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-necib_fifa-2">[2]</a></sup> However, after developing a rapport with future international teammates <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Bouhaddi" title="Sarah Bouhaddi">Sarah Bouhaddi</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89lodie_Thomis" title="Élodie Thomis">Élodie Thomis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laure_Boulleau" title="Laure Boulleau">Laure Boulleau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Houara" title="Jessica Houara">Jessica Houara</a>, and the aforementioned Pizzala, Nécib quickly returned to the form that got her selected to the center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_fifa_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-necib_fifa-2">[2]</a></sup> The CNFE academy is allowed participation in the French women's football league system and, from 2002–2007, fielded a team that participated in the Division 1 Féminine. Nécib spent two seasons with the team and made her league debut on 29 August 2004 against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais_(Ladies)" title="Olympique Lyonnais (Ladies)">Lyon</a>. In the match, she scored the only goal, a 90th-minute winner, in a 1–0 win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Nécib finished the campaign with 20 league appearances and six goals. Four of her six goals came in the final four weeks of the season. On 26 March 2005, she scored a double in a 4–2 defeat to <a href="/wiki/FCF_Juvisy" title="FCF Juvisy">Juvisy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> A week later, she scored the only goal in a win over Olympique Saint-Memmie and, on the final match day of the season, she scored the team's fourth goal in a 5–1 win over Lyon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> CNFE ultimately finished the campaign in 5th-place position. In the following season, Nécib appeared in 18 matches and scored three goals, all of which came in victories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Montpellier">Montpellier</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisa_Cadamuro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Montpellier">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After completing her education and training at Clairefontaine, Nécib returned to the <a href="/wiki/Southern_France" title="Southern France">south of France</a> to sign with Division 1 Féminine club <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montpellier_HSC_(Ladies)" title="Montpellier HSC (Ladies)">Montpellier</a>. She joined the club alongside former Clairefontaine teammate Thomis and made her debut on 3 September 2006 in a 0–0 league draw with <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Toulouse_FC_(Ladies)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Toulouse FC (Ladies) (page does not exist)">Toulouse</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> She scored her first goal for the club two weeks later on 17 September converting a double in a 5–0 away win over USCO Compiègne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> On 8 October, Nécib scored the second goal in a 2–0 victory against <a href="/wiki/ASJ_Soyaux" title="ASJ Soyaux">Soyaux</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> In November, she scored two goals each in wins over FCF Condé-sur-Noireau and <a href="/wiki/FCF_H%C3%A9nin-Beaumont" title="FCF Hénin-Beaumont">Hénin-Beaumont</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Nécib finished the campaign with 11 league goals, which was third-best on the team behind Thomis and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elodie_Ramos" title="Elodie Ramos">Elodie Ramos</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Challenge_de_France" title="Challenge de France">Challenge de France</a>, the women's domestic cup competition in France, Nécib helped Montpellier reach the final where the team faced Lyon. She played the entire match as Montpellier won 3–0 on penalties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The domestic cup title was Nécib's first major honour of her career.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lyon">Lyon</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisa_Cadamuro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Lyon">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the season, on 22 June 2007, Lyon officials announced that the club had signed both Nécib and Thomis to contracts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Nécib was handed the number 14 shirt and made her club debut on 2 September 2007 in the team's opening league match of the campaign; a 4–0 win over <a href="/wiki/ESOF_Vend%C3%A9e_La_Roche-sur-Yon" title="ESOF Vendée La Roche-sur-Yon">La Roche-sur-Yon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> A week later, she scored her first goal for Lyon converting a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_kick_(association_football)" title="Penalty kick (association football)">penalty kick</a> in a 2–0 win against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_F.C._(Ladies)" title="Paris Saint-Germain F.C. (Ladies)">Paris Saint-Germain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Nécib also made her debut in <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">European competition</a> participating in the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_UEFA_Women%27s_Cup" title="2007–08 UEFA Women's Cup">2007–08 edition</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_Women%27s_Cup" title="UEFA Women's Cup">UEFA Women's Cup</a>. On her debut against the women's team of <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovak</a> outfit <a href="/wiki/FK_Slovan_Duslo_%C5%A0a%C4%BEa" title="FK Slovan Duslo Šaľa">Slovan Duslo Šaľa</a> in the group stage, Nécib netted a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hat_trick" title="Hat trick">hat trick</a> in a 12–0 win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> She ultimately finished the European campaign appearing in ten matches and scoring six goals as Lyon reached the semi-finals where the club was eliminated by <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Swedish</a> club <a href="/wiki/Ume%C3%A5_IK" title="Umeå IK">Umeå</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> While simultaneously performing well in Europe, Nécib remained productive in the league scoring in league wins over Toulouse, Hénin-Beaumont, and Soyaux late in the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Lyon eventually pulled away from both Juvisy and Montpellier in the league standings to claim its second straight league title and Nécib's first overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Nécib later helped Lyon capture its third Challenge de France, which completed the club's <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">league and cup double</a> that season. She scored the second goal in a 3–0 win over Paris Saint-Germain in the final match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Louisa_N%C3%A9cib.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3056" data-file-width="4592" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Louisa_N%C3%A9cib.JPG/260px-Louisa_N%C3%A9cib.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Louisa_N%C3%A9cib.JPG/390px-Louisa_N%C3%A9cib.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Louisa_N%C3%A9cib.JPG/520px-Louisa_N%C3%A9cib.JPG 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Louisa_N%C3%A9cib.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Nécib participating in a league match against <a href="/wiki/AS_Montigny-le-Bretonneux" title="AS Montigny-le-Bretonneux">Montigny-le-Bretonneux</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Division_1_F%C3%A9minine" title="2009–10 Division 1 Féminine">2009–10 season</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the infancy of the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Division_1_F%C3%A9minine" title="2008–09 Division 1 Féminine">2008–09 season</a>, Nécib was selected to join the new <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>-based women's soccer league, <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Professional_Soccer" title="Women's Professional Soccer">Women's Professional Soccer</a>, after her American playing rights were assigned to the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Freedom" title="Washington Freedom">Washington Freedom</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2008_WPS_International_Draft" title="2008 WPS International Draft">2008 WPS International Draft</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Her Lyon teammate <a href="/wiki/Sonia_Bompastor" title="Sonia Bompastor">Sonia Bompastor</a> was also assigned to the Freedom. While Bompastor was allowed to negotiate her exit out of the club, Lyon <a href="/wiki/Chairman" title="Chairman">chairman</a> <a href="/wiki/Jean-Michel_Aulas" title="Jean-Michel Aulas">Jean-Michel Aulas</a> was able to convince Nécib to remain in France after having previously declared the player off limits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Nécib scored her first league goal of the campaign on 14 September 2008 in a 12–0 home win over Vendenheim.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> A month later, she scored a double in an 8–1 victory over Soyaux.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Nécib repeated her two-goal display on 1 February 2009 in a 5–0 away win over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/En_Avant_de_Guingamp_(Ladies)" title="En Avant de Guingamp (Ladies)">Stade Briochin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In the UEFA Women's Cup, Nécib scored her first two goals of the campaign in an 8–0 home win over <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austrian</a> club <a href="/wiki/SV_Neulengbach" title="SV Neulengbach">Neulengbach</a> in a second qualifying round group stage match.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> On 18 November, she scored the third goal in a 4–1 second leg win over <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italian</a> club <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A.S.D._C.F._Bardolino_Verona" title="A.S.D. C.F. Bardolino Verona">Bardolino</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> The 9–1 aggregate scoreline advanced Lyon to the semi-finals for the second consecutive season where Lyon were again eliminated, this time by <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> team <a href="/wiki/FCR_2001_Duisburg" title="FCR 2001 Duisburg">FCR 2001 Duisburg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> In the league, Lyon captured its third straight league title, but was unable to defend its Challenge de France title losing to the eventual champions Montpellier in the semi-finals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> For her performances during the campaign, Nécib was named the <a href="/wiki/National_Union_of_Professional_Footballers" title="National Union of Professional Footballers">National Union of Professional Footballers</a> (UNFP) <a href="/wiki/Troph%C3%A9es_UNFP_du_football#Player_of_the_Year_3" title="Trophées UNFP du football">Female Player of the Year</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Division_1_F%C3%A9minine" title="2009–10 Division 1 Féminine">2009–10 season</a>, Nécib switched to the <a href="/wiki/Squad_number_(association_football)" title="Squad number (association football)">number 10 shirt</a> and, due to participating in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Women%27s_Euro_2009" title="UEFA Women's Euro 2009">UEFA Women's Euro 2009</a>, was limited to two substitute appearances in the team's first three matches of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In her first start of the campaign against Soyaux, she scored a double in a 5–0 win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> In the team's first match following the September international break, Nécib scored a goal in the team's 7–1 away win over Toulouse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> In November, while on international duty with France, Nécib suffered an injury and, subsequently, missed five weeks domestically. She returned to the team in the new year in a league match against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AS_Saint-%C3%89tienne_(Ladies)" title="AS Saint-Étienne (Ladies)">Saint-Étienne</a>. In the match, she scored a goal in a 4–0 win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Nécib finished the campaign scoring two goals in the team's final four league matches as Lyon claimed its fourth consecutive league championship and reached the semi-finals of the Challenge de France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> In the re-branded <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Women%27s_Champions_League" title="UEFA Women's Champions League">UEFA Women's Champions League</a>, Nécib made eight appearances scoring four goals as Lyon reached <a href="/wiki/2010_UEFA_Women%27s_Champions_League_Final" title="2010 UEFA Women's Champions League Final">the final</a>. In the semi-finals against Umeå, she converted two goals in a 3–2 first leg victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> The 0–0 draw in the second leg allowed Lyon to advance to the final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> In the penultimate match, Lyon faced <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> club <a href="/wiki/1._FFC_Turbine_Potsdam" title="1. FFC Turbine Potsdam">Turbine Potsdam</a>. Nécib played the entire match in regulation time, but was substituted out prior to the start of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra_time" title="Extra time">extra time</a>. Lyon eventually conceded defeat losing 7–6 on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penalty_shootout_(association_football)" title="Penalty shootout (association football)">penalties</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20130929_-_PSG-Lyon_052.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2498" data-file-width="1665" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/20130929_-_PSG-Lyon_052.jpg/220px-20130929_-_PSG-Lyon_052.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/20130929_-_PSG-Lyon_052.jpg/330px-20130929_-_PSG-Lyon_052.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/20130929_-_PSG-Lyon_052.jpg/440px-20130929_-_PSG-Lyon_052.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20130929_-_PSG-Lyon_052.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Nécib with Lyon in 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For the second time in her career at Lyon, in the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Division_1_F%C3%A9minine" title="2010–11 Division 1 Féminine">2010–11 season</a>, Nécib converted double-digit goals scoring 14, which was third-best on the team behind <a href="/wiki/Sandrine_Br%C3%A9tigny" title="Sandrine Brétigny">Sandrine Brétigny</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eug%C3%A9nie_Le_Sommer" title="Eugénie Le Sommer">Eugénie Le Sommer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> She opened the campaign by scoring in the team's first league match; a 6–0 win over Toulouse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Two weeks later, Nécib scored the second goal in a 3–0 victory against Stade Briochin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> After scoring against La Roche-sur-Yon on 7 November 2010, she went scoreless for two months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> On 9 January 2011, she scored two goals in a 7–0 home win over Hénin-Beaumont.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Two weeks later, Nécib scored another set of goals, this time against Juvisy in a 7–1 win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> In the Challenge de France, she scored in back-to-back rounds against <a href="/wiki/AS_Montigny-le-Bretonneux" title="AS Montigny-le-Bretonneux">Montigny-le-Bretonneux</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rodez_AF" title="Rodez AF">Rodez</a> before playing 53 minutes in a quarter-final defeat on penalties to Juvisy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> On the final match day of the season, despite Lyon clinching its fifth straight league title with several matches to spare, Nécib started the match and scored her first league hat trick in an 8–0 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_UEFA_Women%27s_Champions_League" title="2010–11 UEFA Women's Champions League">2010–11 edition</a> of the Women's Champions League, she scored her only goal of the competition on 4 November 2010 in the first leg of Lyon's Round of 16 tie against <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> club <a href="/wiki/WFC_Rossiyanka" title="WFC Rossiyanka">Rossiyanka</a>. Nécib netted the final goal in a 6–1 away win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> Despite her limited scoring, Lyon still reached <a href="/wiki/2011_UEFA_Women%27s_Champions_League_Final" title="2011 UEFA Women's Champions League Final">the final</a> where the team faced its nemesis Turbine Potsdam. In the final, Nécib started the match and played 55 minutes before being substituted out. Lyon went on to win the match 2–0 to claim its first-ever European title.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the 2011–12 season, Nécib's contract with Lyon expired, which led to speculation that the player would join league rivals Paris Saint-Germain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> However, on 16 July 2012, Nécib re-signed with Lyon after agreeing to a four-year contract with an option for a fifth year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> On May 21, 2016, Lyon confirmed that Louisa Necib and her friend Lotta Schelin departure the club.</p>
<p>In July 2016, she confirmed that she would end her football career after the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Summer Olympics</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisa_Cadamuro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth">Youth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisa_Cadamuro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Youth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Nécib is former France women's youth international having played for her nation at every level for which she was eligible. On 11 September 2003, she was called up to international level for the first time by coach Gérard Sergent to play with the under-17 team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> She played with the team at the 2003 edition of the Nordic Cup, a premier women's youth tournament, before earning a call up to the under-19 team by coach <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Bini" title="Bruno Bini">Bruno Bini</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_federation_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-necib_federation-9">[9]</a></sup> At under-19 level, Nécib featured heavily playing with the team at the <a href="/wiki/La_Manga_Cup" title="La Manga Cup">La Manga Cup</a> and also representing France at the <a href="/wiki/2004_UEFA_Women%27s_Under-19_Championship" title="2004 UEFA Women's Under-19 Championship">2004</a> and <a href="/wiki/2005_UEFA_Women%27s_Under-19_Championship" title="2005 UEFA Women's Under-19 Championship">2005</a> editions of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Women%27s_Under-19_Championship" title="UEFA Women's Under-19 Championship">UEFA Women's Under-19 Championship</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> In the 2004 competition, she appeared in two group stage matches as France suffered elimination in the group stage. In the 2005 edition, Nécib started all five matches France played as the team reached the final. She scored her only goal in the competition in a 4–0 opening group stage victory against <a href="/wiki/Russia_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Russia women's national football team">Russia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> In the final, France faced their group stage opponents Russia and were defeated 6–5 on penalties after the match finished 2–2 in regulation time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>Due to France's second-place finish at the 2005 UEFA Women's Under-19 Championship, the team qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_U-20_Women%27s_World_Championship" title="2006 FIFA U-20 Women's World Championship">2006 FIFA U-20 Women's World Championship</a>, which merited under-20 appearances for Nécib. She made her under-20 debut on 12 August 2006 in a World Cup preparation friendly against <a href="/wiki/Mexico_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Mexico women's national football team">Mexico</a>. In the match, Nécib scored the team's second goal in a 4–2 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> At the World Cup, Nécib appeared in all four matches France contested. In the team's opening group stage match against <a href="/wiki/Argentina_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Argentina women's national football team">Argentina</a>, she scored the team's third goal in a 5–0 win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> France suffered elimination in the quarter-finals losing 2–1 to <a href="/wiki/North_Korea_women%27s_national_football_team" title="North Korea women's national football team">North Korea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Senior">Senior</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisa_Cadamuro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Senior">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FFWM2011_FRA-GER_20110705_imBorussiapark030.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2580" data-file-width="3688" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/FFWM2011_FRA-GER_20110705_imBorussiapark030.jpg/250px-FFWM2011_FRA-GER_20110705_imBorussiapark030.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/FFWM2011_FRA-GER_20110705_imBorussiapark030.jpg/375px-FFWM2011_FRA-GER_20110705_imBorussiapark030.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/FFWM2011_FRA-GER_20110705_imBorussiapark030.jpg/500px-FFWM2011_FRA-GER_20110705_imBorussiapark030.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FFWM2011_FRA-GER_20110705_imBorussiapark030.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Nécib, bottom center, ahead of France's match against Germany at the <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2011 FIFA Women's World Cup">2011 FIFA Women's World Cup</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Prior to playing at the 2005 UEFA Women's Under-19 Championship, Nécib made her senior international debut on 19 February 2005 in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exhibition_match" title="Exhibition match">friendly match</a> against <a href="/wiki/Norway_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Norway women's national football team">Norway</a>. She started the match and was substituted out after 56 minutes as France won 2–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> The victory was France's first-ever against Norway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_federation_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-necib_federation-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Despite featuring in only two senior international matches, the other match being the return leg friendly against Norway on 22 February, Nécib, at the age of 18, was included in the team to play at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Women%27s_Euro_2005" title="UEFA Women's Euro 2005">UEFA Women's Euro 2005</a> by coach Elisabeth Loisel. The midfielder featured in only one match in the competition; the final group stage match against <a href="/wiki/Germany_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Germany women's national football team">Germany</a>. Nécib played the entire match as the Germans won 3–0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-france_germany_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-france_germany-87">[87]</a></sup> In 2010, Nécib admitted that she took the Germany defeat hard stating "I still have regrets because all we needed was a draw and we conceded three goals in ten minutes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_federation_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-necib_federation-9">[9]</a></sup> France had kept the Germans at bay for the majority of the match before letting in three goals in the final 20 minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-france_germany_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-france_germany-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the conclusion of the 2006 U-20 World Cup, Nécib began playing full-time with the senior team participating in <a href="/wiki/2007_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup_qualification" title="2007 FIFA Women's World Cup qualification">qualification matches</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2007_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2007 FIFA Women's World Cup">2007 FIFA Women's World Cup</a>. During the season, Nécib also played with the team at the 2006 edition of the <a href="/wiki/Algarve_Cup" title="Algarve Cup">Algarve Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> On 22 April 2006, she played with the team in a 5–0 World Cup qualification win against <a href="/wiki/Hungary_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Hungary women's national football team">Hungary</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Afterwards, Nécib failed to appear with the team in its final three qualification matches as France missed the World Cup after drawing 1–1 with <a href="/wiki/England_women%27s_national_football_team" title="England women's national football team">England</a> in its final qualifying match. France needed an outright victory to qualify for the tournament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20131031_FR14_Louisa_Necib_9332.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1575" data-file-width="1050" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/20131031_FR14_Louisa_Necib_9332.jpg/220px-20131031_FR14_Louisa_Necib_9332.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/20131031_FR14_Louisa_Necib_9332.jpg/330px-20131031_FR14_Louisa_Necib_9332.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/20131031_FR14_Louisa_Necib_9332.jpg/440px-20131031_FR14_Louisa_Necib_9332.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20131031_FR14_Louisa_Necib_9332.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Nécib playing for France in a match against <a href="/wiki/Austria_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Austria women's national football team">Austria</a> in 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the firing of Loisel and the appointment of former youth national team coach <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Bini" title="Bruno Bini">Bruno Bini</a> in 2007, Nécib became a regular starter in the team and, on 11 April 2007, scored her first international goal in a 6–0 victory over <a href="/wiki/Greece_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Greece women's national football team">Greece</a> in qualification for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Women%27s_Euro_2009" title="UEFA Women's Euro 2009">UEFA Women's Euro 2009</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> She featured as a starter in all seven qualification matches she appeared in and scored another qualification goal in an 8–0 away win over <a href="/wiki/Serbia_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Serbia women's national football team">Serbia</a> on 27 October 2007 as France qualified for the competition with one match to spare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> In the lead up to UEFA Women's Euro 2009, France participated in the 2009 Cyprus Cup. In the competition, Nécib appeared in three matches and scored the team's second goal in a 3–2 group stage win over <a href="/wiki/South_Africa_women%27s_national_football_team" title="South Africa women's national football team">South Africa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> France later finished the competition in third place. Nécib did not participate in the third-place victory over <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_women%27s_national_football_team" title="New Zealand women's national football team">New Zealand</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> After being selected by Bini to participate in Women's Euro 2009, Nécib scored her fourth international goal in a preparation friendly against <a href="/wiki/Scotland_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Scotland women's national football team">Scotland</a> on 12 August 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> In her second major competition for France, Nécib started all four of the team's matches. She scored her first major international goal in the team's opening group stage match against <a href="/wiki/Iceland_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Iceland women's national football team">Iceland</a> netting the final goal in a 3–1 win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> France reached the quarter-finals before suffering elimination losing on penalties to the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Netherlands women's national football team">Netherlands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following Women's Euro 2009, Nécib returned to the national team duty to participate in <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2011 FIFA Women's World Cup qualification (UEFA)">qualification</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2011 FIFA Women's World Cup">2011 FIFA Women's World Cup</a>. In qualification, she participated in nine of the ten qualifying round group stage matches France contested. France finished the stage winning all of its matches and conceding no goals. Nécib scored two goals during the round against <a href="/wiki/Estonia_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Estonia women's national football team">Estonia</a> in a 12–0 win and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Northern Ireland women's national football team">Northern Ireland</a> in a 6–0 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> In September 2010, she played in both legs of France's World Cup playoff match against <a href="/wiki/Italy_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Italy women's national football team">Italy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> France won the tie 3–2 on aggregate to qualify for its second <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="FIFA Women's World Cup">FIFA Women's World Cup</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> On 19 November 2010, Nécib scored her first international double in a 5–0 friendly win over <a href="/wiki/Poland_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Poland women's national football team">Poland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> After playing in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Cyprus_Cup" title="2011 Cyprus Cup">2011 Cyprus Cup</a> and several friendly matches, on 6 June 2011, Nécib was named to the 21-woman squad to participate in the World Cup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> On 18 June, in a prep friendly against <a href="/wiki/Belgium_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Belgium women's national football team">Belgium</a>, she scored her tenth international goal in a 7–0 home win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 26 June 2011, in France's opening World Cup group stage match against <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Nigeria women's national football team">Nigeria</a>, Nécib, on her competition's debut, was named the <i>Player of the Match</i> for her performance in the team's 1–0 victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_ray_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-necib_ray-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> In the team's second group stage match against <a href="/wiki/Canada_women%27s_national_soccer_team" title="Canada women's national soccer team">Canada</a>, she assisted on the final goal, scored by Thomis, in a 4–0 win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Nécib started France's final four matches in the competition, which included a 4–2 loss against Germany in the team final group stage match and a 4–3 penalty shootout victory over England in the quarter-finals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> France were eliminated from the competition in the semi-finals losing 3–1 to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_women%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States women's national soccer team">United States</a> after goals from <a href="/wiki/Abby_Wambach" title="Abby Wambach">Abby Wambach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alex_Morgan" title="Alex Morgan">Alex Morgan</a> broke a 1-1 deadlock created when <a href="/wiki/Sonia_Bompastor" title="Sonia Bompastor">Sonia Bompastor</a> had equalized following Lauren Cheney's opener.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> On 16 July, in the third place match against <a href="/wiki/Sweden_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Sweden women's national football team">Sweden</a>, Nécib was forced to leave the match after 30 minutes due to an injury, a sprained knee who forced her to leave the stadium on crutches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> France lost 2–1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> During and after the competition, Nécib was praised for her performance by several media outlets with one publication declaring that she "was largely responsible for France making it the semifinals in the first place".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_cbc_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-necib_cbc-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_ray_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-necib_ray-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Louisa_Cadamuro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:30%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"Louisa is a player that there are few of. What she does, it's not in the textbooks. She is an artist. It's sunny when she touches the ball. She radiates the team."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;"><small><a href="/wiki/France_women%27s_national_football_team" title="France women's national football team">National team</a> coach <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Bini" title="Bruno Bini">Bruno Bini</a> on Nécib's style of play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_20minutes_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-necib_20minutes-6">[6]</a></sup></small></cite></div>
<p>Nécib primarily plays as an <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Attacking_midfielder" title="Midfielder">attacking midfielder</a>, but can also be deployed in <a href="/wiki/Association_football_positions#Centre_midfielder_.28CM.29" title="Association football positions">central midfield</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Deep-lying_playmaker" title="Midfielder">deep-lying midfielder</a>, or as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Winger" title="Midfielder">winger</a>. Domestically, she primarily plays as a <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">playmaker</a> in the number 10 role, while at international level, she plays as a winger in Bruno Bini's 4–3–3 formation. Two of Nécib's most common exemplary traits are her vision and passing, which have been described as "one-of-a-kind" and "sublime", respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_cbc_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-necib_cbc-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> She is also known for her distinct understanding of the game, which has led to her developing "a great football IQ".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_cbc_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-necib_cbc-3">[3]</a></sup> In addition to her creativity, eye for goal, and tactical awareness, she is known for outstanding control and <a href="/wiki/Dribbling#Association_football" title="Dribbling">dribbling</a> ability, as well as her elegance on the ball.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_fifa_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-necib_fifa-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_cbc_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-necib_cbc-3">[3]</a></sup> Her technical skill and ability to read the game allow her to determine "when to take a defender on one-on-one, how to find a teammate with a slide-rule pass, and how to exploit tight spaces to create scoring chances for herself and her cohorts".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_cbc_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-necib_cbc-3">[3]</a></sup> For these reasons, her playing style has drawn comparisons with compatriot and 1998 World Cup winner Zinedine Zidane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-necib_laprovence2_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-necib_laprovence2-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
